<p><b>Riga</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/iː/ long 'e' in 'seed'">iː</span><span title="'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <span lang="lv" xml:lang="lv"><i>Rīga</i></span>, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Latvian" title="Help:IPA for Latvian">[ˈriːɡa]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<a href="/wiki/File:Lv-R%C4%ABga.ogg" title="File:Lv-Rīga.ogg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a> <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f5/Lv-R%C4%ABga.ogg" class="internal" title="Lv-Rīga.ogg">listen</a>)</small>) is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Latvia" title="Demographics of Latvia">the largest city</a> of <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>. With 696,593 inhabitants (2015), Riga is the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states#Statistics" title="Baltic states">largest city</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a> and home to one third of Latvia's population.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The city lies on the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Riga" title="Gulf of Riga">Gulf of Riga</a>, at the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Daugava_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Daugava (river)">Daugava</a>. Riga's territory covers 307.17&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (118.60&#160;sq&#160;mi) and lies between 1 and 10 <a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">metres</a> (3.3 and 32.8&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Sea_level#Height_above_mean_sea_level" title="Sea level">above sea level</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-RigaMunicipality_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RigaMunicipality-7">[7]</a></sup> on a flat and sandy plain.<sup id="cite_ref-RigaMunicipality_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RigaMunicipality-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Riga was founded in 1201 and is a former <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a> member. Riga's historical centre is a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>, noted for its <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau/Jugendstil</a> architecture and 19th century wooden architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Riga was the <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> during 2014, along with <a href="/wiki/Ume%C3%A5" title="Umeå">Umeå</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>. Riga hosted the <a href="/wiki/2006_Riga_summit" title="2006 Riga summit">2006 NATO Summit</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2003" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2003">Eurovision Song Contest 2003</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2006_Men%27s_World_Ice_Hockey_Championships" title="2006 Men's World Ice Hockey Championships">2006 IIHF Men's World Ice Hockey Championships</a>. It is home to the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union's</a> office of <a href="/wiki/Body_of_European_Regulators_of_Electronic_Communications" title="Body of European Regulators of Electronic Communications">European Regulators for Electronic Communications</a> (BEREC). Riga is served by <a href="/wiki/Riga_International_Airport" title="Riga International Airport">Riga International Airport</a>, the largest airport in the Baltic states.</p>
<p>Riga is a member of <a href="/wiki/Eurocities" title="Eurocities">Eurocities</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> the Union of the Baltic Cities (UBC)<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> and Union of Capitals of the European Union (UCEU).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>One theory for the origin of the name <i>Riga</i> is that it is a corrupted borrowing from the <a href="/wiki/Livonian_language" title="Livonian language">Liv</a> <i>ringa</i> meaning loop, referring to the ancient natural harbour formed by the tributary loop of the Daugava River.<sup id="cite_ref-CEROI_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CEROI-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BCelts_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BCelts-13">[13]</a></sup> The other is that <i>Riga</i> owes its name to this already-established role in commerce between East and West,<sup id="cite_ref-EMA_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-14">[14]</a></sup> as a borrowing of the Latvian <i>rija</i>, for <a href="/wiki/Threshing" title="Threshing">threshing</a> barn, the "j" becoming a "g" in German&#160;— notably, Riga is called <i>Rie</i> by English geographer <a href="/wiki/Richard_Hakluyt" title="Richard Hakluyt">Richard Hakluyt</a> (1589),<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and German historian Dionysius Fabricius (1610) confirms the origin of <i>Riga</i> from <i>rija</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Another theory could be that Riga was named after Riege, the German name for the River Rīdzene, a tributary of the <a href="/wiki/Daugava_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Daugava (river)">Daugava</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>

Right bank of the Daugava</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding">Founding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Founding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The river <a href="/wiki/Daugava_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Daugava (river)">Daugava</a> has been a <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade route</a> since antiquity, part of the <a href="/wiki/Varangians" title="Varangians">Vikings'</a> <a href="/wiki/Trade_route_from_the_Varangians_to_the_Greeks" title="Trade route from the Varangians to the Greeks">Dvina-Dnieper navigation route</a> to Byzantium.<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup> A sheltered <a href="/wiki/Harbor" title="Harbor">natural harbour</a> 15&#160;km (9.3&#160;mi) upriver from the mouth of the Daugava&#160;— the site of today's Riga&#160;— has been recorded, as <i>Duna Urbs</i>, as early as the 2nd century.<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup> It was settled by the <a href="/wiki/Livonian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Livonian people">Livs</a>, an ancient <a href="/wiki/Finnic_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Finnic peoples">Finnic</a> tribe.<sup id="cite_ref-CEROI_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CEROI-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Riga_Buildings.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Old_Riga_Buildings.JPG/220px-Old_Riga_Buildings.JPG" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Old_Riga_Buildings.JPG/330px-Old_Riga_Buildings.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Old_Riga_Buildings.JPG/440px-Old_Riga_Buildings.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2332" data-file-height="2020" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Riga_Buildings.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/House_of_the_Blackheads" title="House of the Blackheads">building of the Brotherhood of Blackheads</a> is one of the most iconic buildings of Old Riga (<a href="/wiki/Vecr%C4%ABga" title="Vecrīga">Vecrīga</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Riga began to develop as a centre of <a href="/wiki/Viking_Age" title="Viking Age">Viking trade during the early Middle Ages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup> Riga's inhabitants occupied themselves mainly with fishing, <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a>, and trading, later developing crafts (in bone, wood, amber, and iron).<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Chronicle_of_Henry" title="Livonian Chronicle of Henry">Livonian Chronicle of Henry</a> testifies to Riga having long been a trading centre by the 12th century, referring to it as <i>portus antiquus</i> (ancient port), and describes dwellings and warehouses used to store mostly corn, flax, and hides.<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup> German traders began visiting Riga, establishing a nearby outpost in 1158.</p>
<p>Along with German traders also arrived the monk <a href="/wiki/Saint_Meinhard" title="Saint Meinhard">Meinhard of Segeberg</a><sup id="cite_ref-EMA_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-14">[14]</a></sup> to convert the Livonian pagans to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>. <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orthodoxy" title="Orthodoxy">Orthodox Christianity</a> had already arrived in Latvia more than a century earlier, and many Latvians baptised.<sup id="cite_ref-EMA_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup> Meinhard settled among the Livs, building a castle and church at <a href="/wiki/Ik%C5%A1%C4%B7ile" title="Ikšķile">Ikšķile</a>, upstream from Riga, and established his bishopric there.<sup id="cite_ref-EMA_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-14">[14]</a></sup> The Livs, however, continued to practice <a href="/wiki/Paganism" title="Paganism">paganism</a> and Meinhard died in Ikšķile in 1196, having failed his mission.<sup id="cite_ref-Saga_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saga-19">[19]</a></sup> In 1198, the <a href="/wiki/Berthold_of_Hanover" title="Berthold of Hanover">Bishop Berthold</a> arrived with a contingent of <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">crusaders</a><sup id="cite_ref-Saga_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saga-19">[19]</a></sup> and commenced a campaign of forced <a href="/wiki/Christianization" title="Christianization">Christianization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EMA_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup> Berthold was killed soon afterwards and his forces defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-Saga_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saga-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Church mobilised to avenge. <a href="/wiki/Pope_Innocent_III" title="Pope Innocent III">Pope Innocent III</a> issued a bull declaring a crusade against the <a href="/wiki/Livonians" title="Livonians">Livonians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Saga_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saga-19">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Albert_of_Riga" title="Albert of Riga">Bishop Albert</a> was proclaimed <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Inflanty" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Inflanty">Bishop of Livonia</a> by his uncle <a href="/wiki/Hartwig_of_Uthlede" title="Hartwig of Uthlede">Hartwig of Uthlede</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Bremen" title="Archbishopric of Bremen">Prince-Archbishop of Bremen and Hamburg</a> in 1199. Albert landed in Riga in 1200<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Saga_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saga-19">[19]</a></sup> with 23 ships<sup id="cite_ref-CathE_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CathE-20">[20]</a></sup> and 500 Westphalian crusaders.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-21">[21]</a></sup> In 1201, he transferred the seat of the Livonian bishopric from Ikšķile to Riga, extorting agreement to do so from the elders of Riga by force.<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Under_Bishop_Albert">Under Bishop Albert</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Under Bishop Albert">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The year 1201 also marked the first arrival of German merchants in Novgorod, via the Dvina.<sup id="cite_ref-PDIntBus_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PDIntBus-22">[22]</a></sup> To defend territory<sup id="cite_ref-RRiga_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RRiga-23">[23]</a></sup> and trade, Albert established the <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Brothers_of_the_Sword" title="Livonian Brothers of the Sword">Order of Livonian Brothers of the Sword</a> in 1202, open to nobles and merchants.<sup id="cite_ref-PDIntBus_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PDIntBus-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Christianization of the Livs continued. In 1207, Albert started on fortification of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-PDIntBus_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PDIntBus-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ORZarina_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ORZarina-24">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Philip_of_Swabia" title="Philip of Swabia">Emperor Philip</a> invested Albert with Livonia as a fief<sup id="cite_ref-HistChristCh_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistChristCh-25">[25]</a></sup> and principality of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup> To promote a permanent military presence, territorial ownership was divided between the Church and the <i>Order</i>, with the Church taking Riga and two-thirds of all lands conquered and granting the <i>Order</i> a third.<sup id="cite_ref-ACQRxlvi_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACQRxlvi-26">[26]</a></sup> Until then, it had been customary for crusaders to serve for a year and then return home.<sup id="cite_ref-ACQRxlvi_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACQRxlvi-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Albert had ensured Riga's commercial future by obtaining papal bulls which decreed that all German merchants had to carry on their Baltic trade through Riga.<sup id="cite_ref-ACQRxlvi_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACQRxlvi-26">[26]</a></sup> In 1211, Riga minted its first coinage,<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup> and Albert laid the cornerstone for the <a href="/wiki/Riga_Cathedral" title="Riga Cathedral">Riga Dom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Riga was not yet secure as an alliance of tribes failed to take Riga.<sup id="cite_ref-ACQRxlvi_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACQRxlvi-26">[26]</a></sup> In 1212, Albert led a campaign to compel <a href="/wiki/Polotsk" title="Polotsk">Polotsk</a> to grant German merchants free river passage.<sup id="cite_ref-PDIntBus_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PDIntBus-22">[22]</a></sup> Polotsk conceded Kukenois (<a href="/wiki/Koknese" title="Koknese">Koknese</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Jersika" title="Principality of Jersika">Jersika</a> to Albert, also ending the Livs' tribute to Polotsk.<sup id="cite_ref-MedChronV_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MedChronV-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Riga's merchant citizenry chafed and sought greater autonomy from the Church. In 1221, they acquired the right to independently self-administer Riga<sup id="cite_ref-RRiga_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RRiga-23">[23]</a></sup> and adopted a city constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-CTHW_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CTHW-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>That same year Albert was compelled to recognise Danish rule over lands they had conquered in Estonia and Livonia.<sup id="cite_ref-CCBF_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCBF-30">[30]</a></sup> Albert had sought the aid of <a href="/wiki/Valdemar_II_of_Denmark" title="Valdemar II of Denmark">King Valdemar of Denmark</a> to protect Riga and Livonian lands against Liv insurrection when reinforcements could not reach Riga. The Danes landed in Livonia, built a fortress at Reval (<a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a>) and set about conquering Estonian and Livonian lands. The Germans attempted, but failed, to assassinate Valdemar.<sup id="cite_ref-EccRevLVI_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EccRevLVI-31">[31]</a></sup> Albert was able to reach an accommodation with them a year later, however and, in 1222, Valdemar returned all Livonian lands and possessions to Albert's control.<sup id="cite_ref-PandBC_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PandBC-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Albert's difficulties with Riga's citizenry continued; with papal intervention, a settlement was reached in 1225 whereby they no longer had to pay tax to the Bishop of Riga,<sup id="cite_ref-LatEnc_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LatEnc-33">[33]</a></sup> and Riga's citizens acquired the right to elect their magistrates and town councillors.<sup id="cite_ref-LatEnc_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LatEnc-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1226, Albert consecrated the Dom Cathedral,<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup> built <a href="/wiki/St._James%27s_Cathedral,_Riga" title="St. James's Cathedral, Riga">St. James's Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BilmanisLIS_15-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilmanisLIS-15">[15]</a></sup> (now a cathedral) and founding a parochial school at the Church of St. George.<sup id="cite_ref-EMA_14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1227, Albert conquered Oesel <sup id="cite_ref-FletcherCoEPC_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FletcherCoEPC-34">[34]</a></sup> and the city of Riga concluded a treaty with the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Smolensk" title="Principality of Smolensk">Principality of Smolensk</a> giving Polotsk to Riga.<sup id="cite_ref-HfT1888_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HfT1888-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Albert died in January 1229.<sup id="cite_ref-FonnesbergPaBC_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FonnesbergPaBC-36">[36]</a></sup> He failed in his aspiration to be anointed archbishop<sup id="cite_ref-HistChristCh_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistChristCh-25">[25]</a></sup> but the German hegemony he established over the Baltic would last for seven centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-ACQRxlvi_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACQRxlvi-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_of_Riga,_1572.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Panorama_of_Riga%2C_1572.jpg/270px-Panorama_of_Riga%2C_1572.jpg" width="270" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Panorama_of_Riga%2C_1572.jpg/405px-Panorama_of_Riga%2C_1572.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Panorama_of_Riga%2C_1572.jpg/540px-Panorama_of_Riga%2C_1572.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2456" data-file-height="999" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_of_Riga,_1572.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Riga in the 16th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hanseatic_League">Hanseatic League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Hanseatic League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1282, Riga became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a>. The Hansa was instrumental in giving Riga economic and political stability, thus providing the city with a strong foundation which endured the political conflagrations that were to come, down to modern times.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Riga_1650.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Riga_1650.jpg/200px-Riga_1650.jpg" width="200" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Riga_1650.jpg/300px-Riga_1650.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Riga_1650.jpg/400px-Riga_1650.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1888" data-file-height="1120" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Riga_1650.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Riga in 1650. The inscription reads: <i>Prospect der Stadt Riga ums Jahr 1650</i> (View at the City of Riga in 1650). Drawing by <a href="/wiki/Johann_Christoph_Brotze" title="Johann Christoph Brotze">Johann Christoph Brotze</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holy_Roman_Empire.2C_Polish.E2.80.93Lithuanian_Commonwealth.2C_the_Swedish_and_Russian_Empires">Holy Roman Empire, Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth, the Swedish and Russian Empires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Holy Roman Empire, Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth, the Swedish and Russian Empires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As the influence of the Hanseatic League waned, Riga became the object of foreign military, political, religious and economic aspirations. Riga accepted the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Reformation</a> in 1522, ending the power of the archbishops. In 1524, <a href="/wiki/Iconoclasm" title="Iconoclasm">iconoclasts</a> targeted a statue of <a href="/wiki/Mary_(mother_of_Jesus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mary (mother of Jesus)">the Virgin Mary</a> in the Cathedral to make a statement against religious icons. It was accused of being a witch, and given a <a href="/wiki/Trial_by_drowning" class="mw-redirect" title="Trial by drowning">trial by water</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Daugava_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Daugava River">Daugava River</a>. The statue floated, so it was denounced as a witch and burnt at Kubsberg.<sup id="cite_ref-fn_1_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fn_1-37">[37]</a></sup> With the demise of the <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Order" title="Livonian Order">Livonian Order</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Livonian_War" title="Livonian War">Livonian War</a>, Riga for twenty years had the status of a <a href="/wiki/Free_imperial_city" title="Free imperial city">Free Imperial City</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> before it came under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Drohiczyn" title="Treaty of Drohiczyn">Treaty of Drohiczyn</a>, which ended the war for Riga in 1581. In 1621, during the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Swedish_War_(1621%E2%80%931625)" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish–Swedish War (1621–1625)">Polish–Swedish War (1621–1625)</a>, Riga and the outlying fortress of <a href="/wiki/Daugavgr%C4%ABva" title="Daugavgrīva">Daugavgriva</a> came under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Adolphus_of_Sweden" title="Gustavus Adolphus of Sweden">Gustavus Adolphus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Sweden" title="Monarchy of Sweden">King of Sweden</a>, who intervened in the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a> not only for political and economic gain but also in favour of German <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a> <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Swedish_War_(1656%E2%80%931658)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Swedish War (1656–1658)">Russo-Swedish War (1656–1658)</a>, Riga withstood a siege by Russian forces.</p>
<p>Riga remained the largest city in Sweden until 1710,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> a period during which the city retained a great deal of autonomous self-government. In that year, in the course of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">Great Northern War</a>, Russia under <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">Tsar</a> <a href="/wiki/Peter_I_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter I of Russia">Peter the Great</a> <a href="/wiki/The_plague_during_the_Great_Northern_War#Lithuania.2C_Livonia.2C_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="The plague during the Great Northern War">besieged plague-stricken Riga</a>. Along with the other Livonian towns and gentry, <a href="/wiki/Capitulation_of_Estonia_and_Livonia" title="Capitulation of Estonia and Livonia">Riga capitulated to Russia</a>, but largely retained their privileges. Riga was made the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Governorate_of_Livonia" title="Governorate of Livonia">Governorate of Riga (later: Livonia)</a>. <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Empire" title="Swedish Empire">Sweden's northern dominance</a> had ended, and Russia's <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">emergence as the strongest Northern power</a> was formalised through the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nystad" title="Treaty of Nystad">Treaty of Nystad</a> in 1721. Riga became an industrialised port city of <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">the Russian empire</a>, in which it remained until <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. By 1900, Riga was the third largest city in Russia after Moscow and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> in terms of the number of industrial workers and number of theatres.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:German_troops_riga_1916.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/German_troops_riga_1916.jpg/200px-German_troops_riga_1916.jpg" width="200" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/German_troops_riga_1916.jpg/300px-German_troops_riga_1916.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/German_troops_riga_1916.jpg/400px-German_troops_riga_1916.jpg 2x" data-file-width="820" data-file-height="515" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:German_troops_riga_1916.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German troops entering Riga during World War I.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During these many centuries of war and changes of power in the Baltic, and despite demographic changes, the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">Baltic Germans</a> in Riga had maintained a dominant position. By 1867, Riga's population was 42.9% German.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Riga employed German as its <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of administration until the installation of Russian in 1891 as the official language in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_governorates" title="Baltic governorates">Baltic provinces</a>, as part of the policy of <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">Russification</a> of the non-Russian speaking territories of the Russian Empire, including <a href="/wiki/Congress_Poland" title="Congress Poland">Congress Poland</a>, Finland and the Baltics, undertaken by Tsar <a href="/wiki/Alexander_III_of_Russia" title="Alexander III of Russia">Alexander III</a>. More and more Latvians started moving to the city during the mid-19th century. The rise of a Latvian <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">bourgeoisie</a> made Riga a centre of the <a href="/wiki/Latvian_National_Awakening" title="Latvian National Awakening">Latvian National Awakening</a> with the founding of the Riga Latvian Association in 1868 and the organisation of the first national song festival in 1873. The <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Movement" title="Nationalist Movement">nationalist movement</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Young_Latvians" title="Young Latvians">Young Latvians</a> was followed by the socialist <a href="/wiki/New_Current" title="New Current">New Current</a> during the city's rapid industrialisation, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/1905_Russian_Revolution" title="1905 Russian Revolution">1905 Revolution</a> led by the <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Social_Democratic_Workers%27_Party" title="Latvian Social Democratic Workers' Party">Latvian Social Democratic Workers' Party</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: World War I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:German_officers_riga_ww1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/German_officers_riga_ww1.jpg/250px-German_officers_riga_ww1.jpg" width="250" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/German_officers_riga_ww1.jpg/375px-German_officers_riga_ww1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/German_officers_riga_ww1.jpg/500px-German_officers_riga_ww1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="806" data-file-height="499" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:German_officers_riga_ww1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
High-ranking German officers and <a href="/wiki/Kaiser_Wilhelm_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaiser Wilhelm II">Kaiser Wilhelm II</a> in Riga after its fall, 3 September 1917.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 20th century brought <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> and the impact of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_(1917)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Revolution (1917)">Russian Revolution of 1917</a> to Riga. In consequence of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jugla" title="Battle of Jugla">battle of Jugla</a>, the <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(German_Empire)" title="German Army (German Empire)">German army</a> marched into Riga on 3 September 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> On 3 March 1918, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk" title="Treaty of Brest-Litovsk">Treaty of Brest-Litovsk</a> was signed, giving the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic countries</a> to Germany. Because of the <a href="/wiki/Armistice_with_Germany_(Compi%C3%A8gne)" class="mw-redirect" title="Armistice with Germany (Compiègne)">Armistice with Germany</a> of 11 November 1918, Germany had to renounce that treaty, as did Russia, leaving Latvia and the other Baltic States in a position to claim independence. Latvia, with Riga as its capital city, thus declared its independence on 18 November 1918. Between World War I and World War II (1918–1940), Riga and Latvia shifted their focus from Russia to the countries of <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>. The United Kingdom and Germany replaced Russia as Latvia's major trade partners. The majority of the Baltic Germans <a href="/wiki/Nazi%E2%80%93Soviet_population_transfers" title="Nazi–Soviet population transfers">were resettled in late 1939</a>, prior to the occupation of Estonia and Latvia by the Soviet Union in June 1940.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Latvia was occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> in June 1940 and then was occupied by <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Latvia_by_Nazi_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupation of Latvia by Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany in 1941–1944</a>. The city's <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Latvia" title="History of the Jews in Latvia">Jewish community</a> was forced into the <a href="/wiki/Riga_Ghetto" title="Riga Ghetto">Riga Ghetto</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi concentration camp">Nazi concentration camp</a> was constructed in <a href="/wiki/Kaiserwald_concentration_camp" title="Kaiserwald concentration camp">Kaiserwald</a>. On 25 October 1941, the Nazis relocated all Jews from Riga and the vicinity to the ghetto. Most of Latvia's Jews (about 24,000) were killed on 30 November and 8 December 1941 in the <a href="/wiki/Rumbula_massacre" title="Rumbula massacre">Rumbula massacre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> By the end of the war, the remaining <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">Baltic Germans</a> were <a href="/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans_(1944%E2%80%9350)#Soviet_Union_and_annexed_territories" title="Flight and expulsion of Germans (1944–50)">expelled to Germany</a>.</p>
<p>The Soviet Red Army re-entered Riga on 13 October 1944. In the following years the massive influx of labourers, administrators, military personnel, and their dependents from Russia and other Soviet republics started. <a href="/wiki/Microdistrict" title="Microdistrict">Microdistricts</a> of the large multi-storied housing blocks were built to house immigrant workers. By 1989, the percentage of Latvians in Riga had fallen to 36.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(December 2011)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In 2004, the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost airlines</a> resulted in cheaper flights from other European cities such as London and Berlin and consequently a substantial increase in numbers of tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2013, <a href="/wiki/Zolit%C5%ABde_shopping_centre_roof_collapse" title="Zolitūde shopping centre roof collapse">the roof of a supermarket collapsed</a>, possibly as a result of the weight of materials used in the construction of a garden on the roof. At least 54 people were killed. The Latvian President Andris Berzins described the disaster as "a large scale murder of many defenceless people".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Riga was the <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> During the Latvia's <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">Presidency of the Council of the European Union</a> in 2015 the 4th <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Partnership" title="Eastern Partnership">Eastern Partnership</a> Summit took place in Riga.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Riga" title="Administrative divisions of Riga">Administrative divisions of Riga</a></div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Central_District,_Riga" title="Central District, Riga">Central District</a> (3&#160;km<sup>2</sup> or 1.2&#160;sq&#160;mi)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kurzeme_District,_Riga" title="Kurzeme District, Riga">Kurzeme District</a> (79&#160;km<sup>2</sup> or 31&#160;sq&#160;mi)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zemgale_Suburb,_Riga" title="Zemgale Suburb, Riga">Zemgale Suburb</a> (41&#160;km<sup>2</sup> or 16&#160;sq&#160;mi)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Northern_District,_Riga" title="Northern District, Riga">Northern District</a> (77&#160;km<sup>2</sup> or 30&#160;sq&#160;mi)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vidzeme_Suburb,_Riga" title="Vidzeme Suburb, Riga">Vidzeme Suburb</a> (57&#160;km<sup>2</sup> or 22&#160;sq&#160;mi)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Latgale_Suburb,_Riga" title="Latgale Suburb, Riga">Latgale Suburb</a> (50&#160;km<sup>2</sup> or 19&#160;sq&#160;mi)</li>
</ul>
<p>Riga's administrative divisions consist of six administrative entities: <a href="/wiki/Central_District,_Riga" title="Central District, Riga">Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurzeme_District,_Riga" title="Kurzeme District, Riga">Kurzeme</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_District,_Riga" title="Northern District, Riga">Northern Districts</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Latgale_Suburb,_Riga" title="Latgale Suburb, Riga">Latgale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vidzeme_Suburb,_Riga" title="Vidzeme Suburb, Riga">Vidzeme</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zemgale_Suburb,_Riga" title="Zemgale Suburb, Riga">Zemgale Suburbs</a>. Three entities were established on 1 September 1941, and the other three were established in October 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-halduskultur_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-halduskultur-46">[46]</a></sup> There are no official lower level administrative units, but the Riga City Council Development Agency is working on a plan, which officially makes Riga consist of 58 neighbourhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-rdpad_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rdpad-47">[47]</a></sup> The current names were confirmed on 28 December 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-CEROI2_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CEROI2-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1208px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Riga_Skyline_Panorama,_Latvia_-_Diliff.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama over Riga from St. Peter's Church"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Riga_Skyline_Panorama%2C_Latvia_-_Diliff.jpg/1200px-Riga_Skyline_Panorama%2C_Latvia_-_Diliff.jpg" width="1200" height="187" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Riga_Skyline_Panorama%2C_Latvia_-_Diliff.jpg/1800px-Riga_Skyline_Panorama%2C_Latvia_-_Diliff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Riga_Skyline_Panorama%2C_Latvia_-_Diliff.jpg/2400px-Riga_Skyline_Panorama%2C_Latvia_-_Diliff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="40000" data-file-height="6223" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Riga_Skyline_Panorama,_Latvia_-_Diliff.jpg" title="File:Riga Skyline Panorama, Latvia - Diliff.jpg"></a></div>
Panorama over Riga from <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Church,_Riga" title="St. Peter's Church, Riga">St. Peter's Church</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The climate of Riga is <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental</a> (Köppen <i>Dfb</i>). The coldest months are January and February, when the average temperature is −5&#160;°C (23&#160;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">°F</a>) but temperatures as low as −20 to −25&#160;°C (−4 to −13&#160;°F) can be observed almost every year on the coldest days. The proximity of the sea causes frequent autumn rains and fogs. Continuous snow cover may last eighty days. The summers in Riga are warm and humid with the average temperature of 18&#160;°C (64&#160;°F), while the temperature on the hottest days can exceed 30&#160;°C (86&#160;°F).</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Riga is one of the key economic and financial centres of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltic States">Baltic States</a>. Roughly half of all the jobs in Latvia are in Riga and the city generates more than 50% of Latvia's GDP as well as around half of Latvia's exports. The biggest exporters are in wood products, IT, food and beverage manufacturing, pharmaceuticals, transport and metallurgy.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Riga Port is one of the largest in the Baltics. It handled a record 34 million tons of cargo in 2011 <sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> and has potential for future growth with new port developments on Krievu Sala.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Tourism is also a large industry in Riga and after a slowdown during the recent global economic recessions, grew 22% in 2011 alone.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:25._trolejbuss_Kri%C5%A1j%C4%81%C5%86a_Valdem%C4%81ra_ielas_un_Kalpaka_bulv%C4%81ra_krustojum%C4%81.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/25._trolejbuss_Kri%C5%A1j%C4%81%C5%86a_Valdem%C4%81ra_ielas_un_Kalpaka_bulv%C4%81ra_krustojum%C4%81.jpg/220px-25._trolejbuss_Kri%C5%A1j%C4%81%C5%86a_Valdem%C4%81ra_ielas_un_Kalpaka_bulv%C4%81ra_krustojum%C4%81.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/25._trolejbuss_Kri%C5%A1j%C4%81%C5%86a_Valdem%C4%81ra_ielas_un_Kalpaka_bulv%C4%81ra_krustojum%C4%81.jpg/330px-25._trolejbuss_Kri%C5%A1j%C4%81%C5%86a_Valdem%C4%81ra_ielas_un_Kalpaka_bulv%C4%81ra_krustojum%C4%81.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/25._trolejbuss_Kri%C5%A1j%C4%81%C5%86a_Valdem%C4%81ra_ielas_un_Kalpaka_bulv%C4%81ra_krustojum%C4%81.jpg/440px-25._trolejbuss_Kri%C5%A1j%C4%81%C5%86a_Valdem%C4%81ra_ielas_un_Kalpaka_bulv%C4%81ra_krustojum%C4%81.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1192" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:25._trolejbuss_Kri%C5%A1j%C4%81%C5%86a_Valdem%C4%81ra_ielas_un_Kalpaka_bulv%C4%81ra_krustojum%C4%81.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
One of the several Trolleybus types in Riga</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Riga, with its central geographic position and concentration of population, has always been the infrastructural hub of Latvia. Several <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Roads_in_Latvia" title="List of National Roads in Latvia">national roads</a> begin in Riga, and <a href="/wiki/European_route_E22" title="European route E22">European route E22</a> crosses Riga from the east and west, while the <a href="/wiki/European_route_E67" title="European route E67">Via Baltica</a> crosses Riga from the south and north.</p>
<p>As a city situated by a river, Riga also has several bridges. The oldest standing bridge is the <a href="/wiki/Railway_Bridge,_Riga" title="Railway Bridge, Riga">Railway Bridge</a>, which is also the only railroad-carrying bridge in Riga. The <a href="/wiki/Stone_Bridge,_Riga" class="mw-redirect" title="Stone Bridge, Riga">Stone Bridge</a> (<i>Akmens tilts</i>) connects <a href="/wiki/Vecr%C4%ABga" title="Vecrīga">Old Riga</a> and <a href="/wiki/P%C4%81rdaugava" title="Pārdaugava">Pārdaugava</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Island_Bridge,_Riga" title="Island Bridge, Riga">Island Bridge</a> (<i>Salu tilts</i>) connects <a href="/wiki/Maskavas_For%C5%A1tate" title="Maskavas Forštate">Maskavas Forštate</a> and Pārdaugava via <a href="/wiki/Za%C4%B7usala" title="Zaķusala">Zaķusala</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Van%C5%A1u_Bridge" title="Vanšu Bridge">Shroud Bridge</a> (<i>Vanšu tilts</i>) connects Old Riga and Pārdaugava via <a href="/wiki/%C4%B6%C4%ABpsala" title="Ķīpsala">Ķīpsala</a>. In 2008, the first stage of the new <a href="/wiki/Southern_Bridge" title="Southern Bridge">Southern Bridge</a> (<i>Dienvidu tilts</i>) route across the Daugava was completed, and was opened to traffic on 17 November.<sup id="cite_ref-rdpad1_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rdpad1-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Southern Bridge was the biggest construction project in the Baltic states in 20 years, and its purpose was to reduce <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">traffic congestion</a> in the city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-dienvidu_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dienvidu-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rdsd_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rdsd-57">[57]</a></sup> Another major construction project is the planned Riga Northern <a href="/wiki/Transport_corridor" title="Transport corridor">Transport Corridor</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-zkoridors_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zkoridors-58">[58]</a></sup> its first segment detailed project was completed in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-rdpad2_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rdpad2-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Freeport_of_Riga" title="Freeport of Riga">Freeport of Riga</a> facilitates cargo and passenger traffic by sea. Sea ferries currently connect <a href="/wiki/Riga_Passenger_Terminal" title="Riga Passenger Terminal">Riga Passenger Terminal</a> to <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a> operated by <a href="/wiki/Tallink" title="Tallink">Tallink</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tallink_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tallink-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Riga,_%C5%A0koda_15T.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Riga%2C_%C5%A0koda_15T.jpg/220px-Riga%2C_%C5%A0koda_15T.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Riga%2C_%C5%A0koda_15T.jpg/330px-Riga%2C_%C5%A0koda_15T.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Riga%2C_%C5%A0koda_15T.jpg/440px-Riga%2C_%C5%A0koda_15T.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<p>Riga has one active airport that serves commercial airlines—the <a href="/wiki/Riga_International_Airport" title="Riga International Airport">Riga International Airport</a> (RIX), built in 1973. Renovation and modernization of the airport was completed in 2001, coinciding with the 800th anniversary of the city. In 2006, a new terminal extension was opened. Extension of the runway was completed in October 2008, and the airport is now able to accommodate large aircraft such as the Airbus A340, Boeing 747, 757, 767 and 777. Another terminal extension is under construction as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The annual number of passengers has grown from 310,000 in 1993 to 4.7 million in 2014, making Riga International Airport the largest in the Baltic States.</p>
<p>The former international airport of Riga, <a href="/wiki/Spilve_Airport" title="Spilve Airport">Spilve Airport</a>, located 5&#160;km (3.11&#160;mi) from Riga city centre, is currently used for small aircraft, pilot training and recreational aviation. Riga was also home to a military air base during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> — <a href="/wiki/Rumbula_Air_Base" title="Rumbula Air Base">Rumbula Air Base</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">Public transportation</a> in the city is provided by <a href="/wiki/R%C4%ABgas_Satiksme" title="Rīgas Satiksme">Rīgas Satiksme</a> which operates a large number of <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">trams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">buses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybuses</a> on an extensive network of routes across the city. In addition, many private owners operate <a href="/wiki/Minibus" title="Minibus">minibus</a> services.</p>
<p>Riga is connected to the rest of Latvia by trains operated by the national carrier <a href="/wiki/Passenger_Train_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Passenger Train (company)">Passenger Train</a>, whose headquarters are in Riga. There are also international rail services to <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, and plans to revive passenger rail traffic with <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Trans-European_Transport_Networks" title="Trans-European Transport Networks">TEN-T</a> project called <a href="/wiki/Rail_Baltica" title="Rail Baltica">Rail Baltica</a> envisages building a <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed railway</a> line via Riga connecting <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a> to <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> using <a href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" title="Standard gauge">standard gauge</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> expected to be put into operation in 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Riga_International_Coach_Terminal" title="Riga International Coach Terminal">Riga International Coach Terminal</a> provides domestic and international connections by <a href="/wiki/Coach_(vehicle)" class="mw-redirect" title="Coach (vehicle)">coach</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Riga_City_Council" title="Riga City Council">Riga City Council</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Riga_-_City_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Riga_-_City_Hall.jpg/220px-Riga_-_City_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Riga_-_City_Hall.jpg/330px-Riga_-_City_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Riga_-_City_Hall.jpg/440px-Riga_-_City_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Riga_-_City_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Riga_City_Council" title="Riga City Council">Riga City Council</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The head of the city government in Riga is the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Riga" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor of Riga">mayor</a>. Incumbent mayor <a href="/wiki/Nils_U%C5%A1akovs" title="Nils Ušakovs">Nils Ušakovs</a>, who is a member of the <i><a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_%22Harmony%22" title="Social Democratic Party &quot;Harmony&quot;">Harmony</a></i> party, took office on 1 July 2009.</p>
<p>The city council is a democratically elected institution and is the final decision-making authority in the city. The Council consists of 60 members who are elected every four years. The Presidium of the Riga City Council consists of the Chairman of the Riga City Council and the representatives delegated by the political parties or party blocks elected to the City Council.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>With 641,000 inhabitants in 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-population_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-population-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Riga is the largest city in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic States</a>, though its population has decreased from just over 900,000 in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-population_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-population-3">[3]</a></sup> Notable causes include <a href="/wiki/Emigration" title="Emigration">emigration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ageing_of_Europe" title="Ageing of Europe">low birth rates</a>. Some have estimated that the population may fall by as much as 50% by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> According to the 2011 census data, ethnic Latvians made up 49.33% of the population of Riga, with the percentage of ethnic Russians at 37.21%, Belarusians at 3.88%, Ukrainians at 3.45%, Poles at 1.85%, Lithuanians at 0.83% and other ethnicities at 3.46%. By comparison, 67.1% of Latvia's total population are ethnic <a href="/wiki/Latvian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Latvian people">Latvians</a>, 21.9% are <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, 3.3% are <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a>, 2.2% are <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, 2.2% are <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Polish</a>, 1.2% are <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithuanian people">Lithuanians</a> and the remaining 2.1% are accounted for by other ethnicities.<sup id="cite_ref-csb.gov.lv_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csb.gov.lv-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Upon the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Latvia#Restoration_of_independence" title="History of Latvia">restoration of Latvia's independence in 1991</a>, Soviet era immigrants (and any of their offspring born before 1991) were not automatically granted Latvian citizenship because they had migrated to the territory of Latvia during the years when Latvia was part of the Soviet Union. In 2013 citizens of Latvia made up 73.1%, <a href="/wiki/Non-citizens_(Latvia)" title="Non-citizens (Latvia)">non-citizens</a> 21.9% and citizens of other countries 4.9% of the population of Riga.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The proportion of ethnic Latvians in Riga increased from 36.5% in 1989 to 42.4% in 2010. In contrast, the percentage of Russians fell from 47.3% to 40.7% in the same time period. Latvians overtook Russians as the largest ethnic group in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicity_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicity-4">[4]</a></sup> Further projections show that the ethnic Russian population will continue a steady decline.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_population_figures">Historic population figures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Historic population figures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Riga_Radio_and_TV_Tower" title="Riga Radio and TV Tower">radio and TV tower</a> of Riga is the tallest structure in Latvia and the Baltic States, and one of the tallest in the European Union, reaching 368.5&#160;m (1,209&#160;ft). Riga centre also has many great examples of <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> architecture, as well as a medieval old town.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_Nouveau">Art Nouveau</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Art Nouveau">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau_architecture_in_Riga" title="Art Nouveau architecture in Riga">Art Nouveau architecture in Riga</a></div>
<p>It is generally recognized that Riga has the finest and the largest collection of <a href="/wiki/Art_nouveau" class="mw-redirect" title="Art nouveau">art nouveau</a> buildings in the world. This is due to the fact that at the end of the 19th and beginning of the 20th centuries, when Art Nouveau was at the height of its popularity, Riga experienced an unprecedented financial and demographic boom.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (March 2015)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup> In the period from 1857 to 1914 its population grew from 282,000 to 558,000 making it the 4th largest city in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Saint-Petersburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint-Petersburg">Saint-Petersburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>) and its largest port. The bourgeoisie of Riga used their wealth to build imposing apartment blocks around the former <a href="/wiki/City_walls" class="mw-redirect" title="City walls">city walls</a>. Local architects, mostly graduates of <a href="/wiki/Riga_Technical_University" title="Riga Technical University">Riga Technical University</a>, adopted current European movements, and in particular Art Nouveau.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (March 2015)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup> In that period around 800 Art Nouveau buildings were erected.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The majority of them are concentrated in the central part of Riga and a few more in the Old Town.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Riga_iedvesmas_pilseta.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b0/Riga_iedvesmas_pilseta.png/250px-Riga_iedvesmas_pilseta.png" width="250" height="79" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b0/Riga_iedvesmas_pilseta.png/375px-Riga_iedvesmas_pilseta.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b0/Riga_iedvesmas_pilseta.png 2x" data-file-width="441" data-file-height="140" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Riga_iedvesmas_pilseta.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The logo for the city of Riga, designed for its 800th anniversary (it means <i>Riga: City of inspiration</i>).</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatres">Theatres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Theatres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Latvian_National_Opera" title="Latvian National Opera">Latvian National Opera</a> was founded in 1918. The repertoire of the theatre embraces all opera masterpieces. The Latvian National Opera is famous not only for its operas, but for its ballet troupe as well.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Latvian_National_Theatre" title="Latvian National Theatre">Latvian National Theatre</a> was founded in 1919. The Latvian National Theatre preserves the traditions of <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Latvia" title="Culture of Latvia">Latvian</a> <a href="/wiki/Drama_school" title="Drama school">drama school</a>. It is one of the biggest theatres in Latvia.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Riga Russian Theatre is the oldest professional drama theatre in Latvia, established in 1883. The repertoire of the theatre includes classical plays and experimental performances of Russian and other foreign playwrights.<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.trd.lv/eng">Riga Russian Theatre</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Daile_Theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Daile Theatre">Daile Theatre</a> was opened for the first time in 1920. It is one of the most successful theatres in Latvia. This theatre is distinguished by its frequent productions of modern foreign plays.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li>Latvian State Puppet Theatre was founded in 1944. This theatre presents shows for children and adults.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/New_Riga_Theatre" title="New Riga Theatre">New Riga Theatre</a> was opened in 1992. It has an intelligent and attractive repertoire of high quality that focused on a modern, educated and socially active audience.</li>
</ul>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
<div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Choir_Games">World Choir Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: World Choir Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Riga hosted the biannual 2014 <a href="/wiki/World_Choir_Games" title="World Choir Games">World Choir Games</a> from 9–19 July 2014 which coincided with the city being named <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> for 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-interkultur.com_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interkultur.com-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The event, organised by the choral foundation, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Interkultur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Interkultur (page does not exist)">Interkultur</a>, takes place at various host cities every two years and was originally known as the "Choir Olympics".<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The event regularly sees over 15'000 choristers in over 300 choirs from over 60 nations compete for gold, silver and bronze medals in over 20 categories. The competition is further divided into a Champions Competition and an Open Competition to allow choirs from all backgrounds to enter.<sup id="cite_ref-interkultur.com_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interkultur.com-72">[72]</a></sup> Choral workshops and festivals are also witnessed in the host cities and are usually open to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Riga has a rich basketball history. In the 1950s <a href="/wiki/ASK_Riga" title="ASK Riga">ASK Riga</a> became the best club in the Soviet Union and also in Europe, winning the first three editions of the <a href="/wiki/Euroleague" class="mw-redirect" title="Euroleague">European Cup for Men's Champions Clubs</a> from 1958 to 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1960, ASK was not the only team from Riga to take the European crown. <a href="/wiki/TTT_Riga" title="TTT Riga">TTT Riga</a> clinched their first title in the <a href="/wiki/EuroLeague_Women" title="EuroLeague Women">European Cup for Women's Champion Clubs</a>, turning Riga into the capital city of European basketball because for the first and, so far, only time in the history of European basketball, clubs from the same city were concurrent European Men's and Women's club champions.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Riga was one of the hosts for <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket_2015" title="EuroBasket 2015">EuroBasket 2015</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_clubs">Sports clubs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sports clubs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/BK_VEF_R%C4%ABga" title="BK VEF Rīga">BK VEF Rīga</a> – a professional basketball team that is a three-time <a href="/wiki/Latvijas_Basketbola_l%C4%ABga" title="Latvijas Basketbola līga">Latvian champion</a>. VEF also participates in high-level international competition such as <a href="/wiki/Eurocup_Basketball" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurocup Basketball">Eurocup</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barons_LMT" class="mw-redirect" title="Barons LMT">Barons LMT</a> – a men's basketball team, two-time <a href="/wiki/Latvijas_Basketbola_l%C4%ABga" title="Latvijas Basketbola līga">Latvian champion</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/EuroCup_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="EuroCup 2007–08">2008</a> <a href="/wiki/FIBA_EuroCup" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA EuroCup">FIBA EuroCup</a> winner</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TTT_Riga" title="TTT Riga">TTT Riga</a> – a women's basketball team, which between 1960 and 1982 won eighteen <a href="/wiki/FIBA_EuroLeague_Women" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA EuroLeague Women">FIBA EuroLeague Women</a> titles</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">Ice hockey</a>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dinamo_Riga" title="Dinamo Riga">Dinamo Riga</a> – a professional ice hockey club established in 2008. It plays in the <a href="/wiki/Kontinental_Hockey_League" title="Kontinental Hockey League">Kontinental Hockey League</a>. Dinamo was established as a successor to the <a href="/wiki/Dinamo_Riga_(original)" title="Dinamo Riga (original)">former hockey team with the same name</a>, which was founded in 1946 but ceased to exist in 1995.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HK_Riga" class="mw-redirect" title="HK Riga">HK Riga</a> – a junior hockey club, playing in the <a href="/wiki/Minor_Hockey_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor Hockey League">Minor Hockey League</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Skonto_FC" title="Skonto FC">Skonto FC</a> – a football club established in 1991. The club won fourteen successive <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Higher_League" title="Latvian Higher League">Latvian Higher League</a> titles. For a long time it provided the core of the <a href="/wiki/Latvian_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Latvian national football team">Latvian national football team</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/FS_Metta-LU" class="mw-redirect" title="FS Metta-LU">FS Metta-LU</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_facilities">Sports facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sports facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skonto_Stadions.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Skonto_Stadions.jpg/220px-Skonto_Stadions.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Skonto_Stadions.jpg/330px-Skonto_Stadions.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Skonto_Stadions.jpg/440px-Skonto_Stadions.jpg 2x" data-file-width="597" data-file-height="400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skonto_Stadions.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Skonto_Stadium" title="Skonto Stadium">Skonto Stadium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arena_Riga" title="Arena Riga">Arena Riga</a> – a multi-purpose arena built in 2006 as the main venue for the <a href="/wiki/2006_Men%27s_World_Ice_Hockey_Championships" title="2006 Men's World Ice Hockey Championships">2006 Men's World Ice Hockey Championships</a>. It can hold up to 14,500 people and has hosted <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> events, as well as <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_X-Fighters" title="Red Bull X-Fighters">Red Bull X-Fighters</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Skonto_Stadium" title="Skonto Stadium">Skonto Stadium</a> – a football stadium, built in 2000. It is the main stadium used for games of the <a href="/wiki/Latvian_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Latvian national football team">Latvian national football team</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Daugava_Stadium_(Riga)" title="Daugava Stadium (Riga)">Daugava Stadium</a> – a stadium built in 1958, used for both <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Latvijas_Universitates_Stadions" title="Latvijas Universitates Stadions">Latvijas Universitates Stadions</a></li>
<li>Biķernieku Kompleksā Sporta Bāze – Latvia's leading <a href="/wiki/Motorsport" title="Motorsport">motorsport</a> complex</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_Sister_cities">Twin towns – Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Twin towns – Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td colspan="2"></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2">
<div>
<ul>
<li><span style="position: relative; top: 0.2em;"><sup>1</sup></span>&#160;Also the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a></li>
<li><span style="position: relative; top: 0.2em;"><sup>2</sup></span>&#160;Also the seat of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, see <a href="/wiki/Institutional_seats_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutional seats of the European Union">Institutional seats of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brussels_and_the_European_Union" title="Brussels and the European Union">Brussels and the European Union</a></li>
<li><span style="position: relative; top: 0.2em;"><sup>3</sup></span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">Transcontinental country</a></li>
<li><span style="position: relative; top: 0.2em;"><sup>4</sup></span>&#160;Entirely in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Southwest Asia</a> but having socio-political connections with Europe</li>
<li><span style="position: relative; top: 0.2em;"><sup>5</sup></span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">Partially recognised country</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>

<li><sup><small>1</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a> were both capital of the Westphalian Quarter at different times.</li>
<li><sup><small>2</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> gained importance once <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a> became inaccessible due to the silting of the <a href="/wiki/Zwin" title="Zwin">Zwin</a> channel.</li>
